Another vision, conferred upon Wambert while he was awake, seems to tell us that an angel appeared to him in the form of an enormous eagle-see [Laurent] Sauer, the Life of St Bertulf, chapter 12, under 5th January-although if anyone were to argue that this was a real bird, (as it seems was the one Bishop Noger writes about in The Translation of St Laudoaldus, in Sauer, volume 2), I should not particularly object.³⁸¹

<div align="center"><b>Catullus Troubled by Spirits of the Slaughtered</b></div>
<div align="center">"Martin Del Rio - Investigations Into Magic Volume 2" Page 144</div>
Josephus was of this opinion, as much because he thought the soul of Samuel really did appear as because he says that [Marcus Valerius] Catullus had been dreadfully troubled by the spirits of the men he had slaughtered.

<div align="center"><b>The Apparition of Samuel to Saul</b></div>
<div align="center">"Martin Del Rio - Investigations Into Magic Volume 2" Pages 145-146</div>
It is proved in the time of the Old Testament because Samuel's soul appeared to Saul, not because it has been roused by the power of a magical incantation, but because it has been sent by God. This appears to be the more accurate opinion. God sent Samuel to reprove the disobedient king, threaten him with immediate punishment, and so encourage him to repent. And after this he fell asleep and showed and made known to the King the end of his life. He lifted up his voice from the earth in prophecy to destroy the ungodliness of the nation.

<div align="center"><b>Apparitions to Garlanded Christians in Tertullian's Time</b></div>
<div align="center">"Martin Del Rio - Investigations Into Magic Volume 2" Pages 146-146</div>
Likewise we read that because they had garlanded the doorways [of houses], similar apparitions happened not infrequently to Christians in the time of Tertullian for the sake of getting these sinners to ask to be set free [from their slavery to the Devil].

<div align="center"><b>Natalius Scourged by Angels</b></div>
<div align="center">"Martin Del Rio - Investigations Into Magic Volume 2" Pages 146-146</div>
Eusebius tells us that Natalius was scourged by angels in the same way because he had attached himself to a group of heretics.

<div align="center"><b>Citizen of Hippo Warned for False Oath</b></div>
<div align="center">"Martin Del Rio - Investigations Into Magic Volume 2" Pages 146-146</div>
St Augustine tells a similar story, as though it were well known to him, about a citizen of Hippo [who received warnings] because he was accused of breaking an oath by swearing falsely.

<div align="center"><b>Bishop Lawrence Scourged by St Peter</b></div>
<div align="center">"Martin Del Rio - Investigations Into Magic Volume 2" Pages 146-146</div>
Bede testifies that when Lawrence, Bishop of Canterbury, was thinking about running away from his flock, he was scourged by St Peter.

<div align="center"><b>Blessed Virgin Punishes the Landlord</b></div>
<div align="center">"Martin Del Rio - Investigations Into Magic Volume 2" Pages 146-146</div>
During the reign of the Emperor Maurice, the Blessed Virgin appeared to a landlord while he was asleep and ploughed round his knees with a switch because he had not thrown blasphemers out of his guest-house, and in the morning it was found that his shin-bones had been sundered from his legs.

<div align="center"><b>Moses Appears on Mount Tabor</b></div>
<div align="center">"Martin Del Rio - Investigations Into Magic Volume 2" Pages 147-147</div>
A still clearer [example], as St Augustine says, is that of Moses who appeared with Christ our Lord on Mt Tabor, even though he really was deadSt Augustine thinks it quite likely [he appeared] in an assumed body made out of air-

<div align="center"><b>Jeremiah and Onias Appear to Judas Maccabaeus</b></div>
<div align="center">"Martin Del Rio - Investigations Into Magic Volume 2" Pages 147-147</div>
A third example is that of Jeremiah and Onias who appeared to Judas Maccabaeus,

<div align="center"><b>Christ's Post-Resurrection Appearance Thought to Be a Spirit</b></div>
<div align="center">"Martin Del Rio - Investigations Into Magic Volume 2" Pages 147-147</div>
After His resurrection, Christ our Lord came to the Apostles even though the doors were closed, something they did not think possible unless it was done by a spirit [spiritu]. They thought they were seeing a spirit and were therefore extremely disturbed and terrified. Indeed, Theophilus expressly declares that they thought it was some soul which had come back from another life. St Augustine, Eucherius, Bede, Cardinal Hugo, and many others had the same idea, but they thought it was Christ’s soul in an assumed body [made of air, not His own body, and that [the Apostles] were not yet certain He had risen again. Christ knew what they were thinking and replied that by touching His real body they could know He was not a spirit.

<div align="center"><b>Apostles See Christ Walking on Water as a Spirit</b></div>
<div align="center">"Martin Del Rio - Investigations Into Magic Volume 2" Pages 147-147</div>
The Apostles had had the same suspicion and fear before the Passion when they saw Him walking on water. They had been reproved on that occasion, not because they thought that ghosts [spectra] sometimes do exist, but because they thought it was not Christ who was then appearing to them.

<div align="center"><b>Rhoda Sees Peter's Apparition</b></div>
<div align="center">"Martin Del Rio - Investigations Into Magic Volume 2" Pages 147-147</div>
When Rhoda told the whole Church which was in Jerusalem that Peter had been freed from prison and was standing at the gate, [Acts 12.1415] they said she was mad, because they were fully persuaded that Peter was alive and being kept in prison. They knew the soul of a living person could not appear outwith his body, and so they rebuked the girl’s mistake [in thinking] it was the soul of a living person. They thought it was an angel disguised as Peter. Had they believed Peter was dead, they would have agreed with the girl.

<div align="center"><b>Apparition of the Virgin Mary to St James at Zaragoza</b></div>
<div align="center">"Martin Del Rio - Investigations Into Magic Volume 2" Pages 148-148</div>
We had the first church in Spain, perhaps in the whole of Europe, dedicated by St James, son of Zebedee, to the Mother of God, St Mary of the Pillar, near the Ebro at Zaragoza. This was reported in the annals of Celtiberia and also accepted by such a firm tradition of the church there that no Catholic in that area has any doubts about it. The tradition is that the Blessed Virgin appeared to the Apostle of Spain standing on a pillar and ordered him to dedicate a small shrine to her on that spot. It is now a rich and noble church.

<div align="center"><b>Christ Appears to St Peter Fleeing Persecution</b></div>
<div align="center">"Martin Del Rio - Investigations Into Magic Volume 2" Pages 148-148</div>
Christ showed Himself unmistakably to St Peter while \[Peter\] was running away from persecution, and said He was taking Himself off to Rome to be crucified again. Peter understood what the Lord meant, turned back, and was taken to a cross. So, this is how Christ was crucified again in Peter.

<div align="center"><b>Jesus Appears to Carpus of Crete</b></div>
<div align="center">"Martin Del Rio - Investigations Into Magic Volume 2" Pages 148-148</div>
In letter 8, addressed to Demophilus, \[section 6\], St Dionysius the Areopagite tells us that Jesus, accompanied by many angels, appeared to Carpus of Crete and rebuked him because he was looking for the punishment of a lapsed brother, someone who was leading people astray;

<div align="center"><b>St Martial Sees Soul of St Valeria</b></div>
<div align="center">"Martin Del Rio - Investigations Into Magic Volume 2" Pages 148-149</div>
and during the reign of the Emperor Vespasian, there lived St Martial, Bishop of Limoges, a disciple of Christ. He saw the soul of the martyr St Valeria going up to Heaven like a bright flame. (This story is told in the Acts of St Martial in \[Laurent Sauer\]).

<div align="center"><b>St Potamiaena Appears to Basilides</b></div>
<div align="center">"Martin Del Rio - Investigations Into Magic Volume 2" Pages 149-149</div>
There is no doubt that in Origen\'s time, St Potamiaena appeared to Basilides, her executioner, and converted him to the Faith, and not only him, but several others, too, as Eusebius tells us in his \[History of the Church\] Book 6, chapter 4;

<div align="center"><b>Spirits Convert People Through Visions</b></div>
<div align="center">"Martin Del Rio - Investigations Into Magic Volume 2" Pages 149-149</div>
and Origen himself, in Against Celsus Book 1, \[chapter 46\], testifies, \'Many have been brought to the Christian religion, more or less unwillingly, by some kind of spirit \[spiritu\] which suddenly changed their mind in such a way that, after they had been shown visions either while they were asleep or while they were awake, they would then not hesitate to go to meet death on behalf of the Word whom they had hated. I have seen many such instances, and if, in what I am writing here, I were to recount merely what they did, unbelievers would start to jeer, thinking I was making it up just like those they wrongly suspect are doing so. God, however, is witness to my conscience that I am trying to make people favourable towards Jesus\'s teaching, not by telling deceitful anecdotes, but by giving true examples.\'

<div align="center"><b>St John the Evangelist and Virgin Mary Appear to St Gregory the Miracle-Worker</b></div>
<div align="center">"Martin Del Rio - Investigations Into Magic Volume 2" Pages 150-150</div>
St John the Evangelist, along with the Mother of God, appeared to St Gregory the Miracle-Worker, as St Gregory of Nyssa, \[Gregory\'s\] very important biographer, tells us in a style which may be accurate, but is also long-winded.

<div align="center"><b>Martyred Son of St Quartillosa Appears</b></div>
<div align="center">"Martin Del Rio - Investigations Into Magic Volume 2" Pages 150-150</div>
The martyred son of St Quartillosa appeared and confirmed that his mother had been martyred. The story is told in the letter of African confessors which Laurent Sauer produced in Vol. 1, under 24th February, and in an expansion to it,

<div align="center"><b>St Cyprian Appears to Montanus and Flavianus</b></div>
<div align="center">"Martin Del Rio - Investigations Into Magic Volume 2" Pages 150-150</div>
St Cyprian, too, is said to have appeared to the confessors Montanus and Flavianus to encourage them.

<div align="center"><b>St Cyprian Appears to Marianus</b></div>
<div align="center">"Martin Del Rio - Investigations Into Magic Volume 2" Pages 150-150</div>
Other authentic Acts of the Martyrs of Sidra, reproduced by Sauer, (Volume 3, under ist May), say that St Cyprian appeared to Marianus and stretched out his hand,

<div align="center"><b>Child-Martyr Appears to Agapius</b></div>
<div align="center">"Martin Del Rio - Investigations Into Magic Volume 2" Pages 150-150</div>
and that a child-martyr was seen by Agapius just before \[the child\] received his crown \[of martyrdom\].

<div align="center"><b>St Agnes Appears to Her Parents</b></div>
<div align="center">"Martin Del Rio - Investigations Into Magic Volume 2" Pages 150-150</div>
In sermon 90, St Ambrose says that St Agnes appeared to her parents while they were keeping constant vigil one night at her tomb. She was accompanied by a large number of virgins and spoke to \[her parents as follows. \'Please don\'t mourn me now that I am dead, Mother and Father, because I am alive in Heaven with these virgins in the presence of Him whom I loved with all my heart \[while I was\] on earth\'.

<div align="center"><b>St Agnes Appears to Constantia</b></div>
<div align="center">"Martin Del Rio - Investigations Into Magic Volume 2" Pages 150-150</div>
\[Sauer\] adds that several years later, while Constantia was asleep, \[St Agnes\] promised her health and fulfilled her promise.

<div align="center"><b>St Peter Appears to St Agatha</b></div>
<div align="center">"Martin Del Rio - Investigations Into Magic Volume 2" Pages 150-150</div>
Earlier, too, during the reign of Decius, St Peter appeared to St Agatha in prison, and restored her breast to her. (Acts of St Agatha, under 5th February, in Sauer.)

<div align="center"><b>St Agnes Appears to St Lucia</b></div>
<div align="center">"Martin Del Rio - Investigations Into Magic Volume 2" Pages 150-150</div>
Later, \[St Agnes\] appeared to St Lucia and freed her mother Eutychia from a bloody flux, (Acts of St Lucia, under 13th December, in Sauer).

<div align="center"><b>Christ Appears to St Peter of Alexandria</b></div>
<div align="center">"Martin Del Rio - Investigations Into Magic Volume 2" Pages 150-150</div>
After 300AD, or Fourth Century Christ our Lord deigned to appear to St Peter of Alexandria in the form of a child looking for its clothes which had been torn by Arius, (Sauer, Volume 6, under 15th November).

<div align="center"><b>Apostles Peter and Paul Appear to Constantine</b></div>
<div align="center">"Martin Del Rio - Investigations Into Magic Volume 2" Pages 150-151</div>
In Volume 2 of his letters and decretals, \[Pope\] Hadrian says that in the prefaces to Synod VII, or the Second Council of Nicaea, Acts 2, after the blessed Emperor Constantine was converted to the Christian faith, one reads the following: \'When the day was at an end and silence fell and it was time to go to sleep, lo and behold, the holy Apostles, Peter and Paul, suddenly appeared to the King, saying, \"Since you have put an end to your disgraceful crimes and have developed a horror of shedding the blood of innocents, we have been sent by the Lord Jesus Christ to give you advice on how to recover soundness of mind. So, you have heard our warnings\", etc.

<div align="center"><b>Virgin Mary Appears to Church Architect</b></div>
<div align="center">"Martin Del Rio - Investigations Into Magic Volume 2" Pages 150-150</div>
The following also happened. When Constantine ordered the building of a church for the Mother of God. She herself appeared to the architect and instructed him where the pillars could be erected. (Gregory of Tours, The Glory of the Martyrs, chapter 8).

<div align="center"><b>Spiridion and Tryphillus Appear to Constantius</b></div>
<div align="center">"Martin Del Rio - Investigations Into Magic Volume 2" Pages 150-150</div>
Spiridion and Tryphillus earlier appeared to Constantius while he was asleep and cured him, and yet they were still alive. (From \[St Simeon\] Metaphrastes in Sauer, Volume 6, under 12th December).

<div align="center"><b>Irene Speaks from Her Tomb to Spiridion</b></div>
<div align="center">"Martin Del Rio - Investigations Into Magic Volume 2" Pages 150-151</div>
Socrates, (\[History of the Church\] Book 1, chapter 8 \[12\]) and Rufinus, (\[History of the Church\] Book 1, chapter 5), say this in connection with that same Spiridion. Let me quote what Rufinus says. \'He had a daughter called Irene and when she had looked after him well, she died, a virgin. After her death, someone came along saying he had entrusted something to her keeping. Her father said he had no knowledge of this, \[but\] he searched the whole house diligently. He did not find what he was looking for anywhere, but the man who had entrusted it \[to Irene\] persisted and went on pressing the matter with wailing and tears. He kept swearing he would put an end to his life unless he recovered what he had entrusted to her. Moved by the man\'s tears, the elderly \[father\] hurried off to his daughter\'s tomb and started calling her by name. Then, from the tomb, she said, \"What do you want, Father?\" \"Where did you put what that man entrusted to you?\" he asked. She told him where it was. \"You will find it buried there\", she said. He went back home, found the object, just as his daughter had told him from the tomb in answer to his question, and handed it back to the man who had kept on asking for it\'.

<div align="center"><b>Dead Bishops Chrysanthus and Musonius Sign Synod Decree</b></div>
<div align="center">"Martin Del Rio - Investigations Into Magic Volume 2" Pages 151-151</div>
Gregory of Caesarea, a priest, reported an extraordinary story. (See \[Luigi\] Lippomano, Volume 6, \'A Discourse on the Synod of Nicaea\'.) \'Two holy bishops\', he said, \'Chrysanthus and Musonius, had not yet appended their signatures to \[the Synod\'s\] decree, and it happened that, by divine providence, they departed this human life. So, the holy fathers \[of the Synod\] came to the place where \[the two bishops\] were sleeping together \[in death\], and once \[the Fathers\] were with them, \[the bishops\] heard what was being said. \"Brethren and fathers\", said \[the Synod Fathers\], \"you have fought a magnificent fight along with us, you have finished the race, you have preserved the Faith. So, if you decide that what \[the Synod\] has done is pleasing to God, (because you now perceive \[things\] in a purer way), let there be nothing to stop you from signing this decree as well\". They all said this together, put their seals on the decree, put it in the bishops\' coffin, and spent the whole of that night awake in prayer. Next day, when they came to the coffin, they found that the seals they had attached \[to the decree had been broken, and when they unrolled the holy decree, they found that the holy bishops\' signatures had been added to it\'. Nicephorus, (\[History of the Church\] Book 8, chapter 23), adds the words which had been written at the bottom. \'Chrysanthus and Musonius. We took part in the first holy ecumenical Synod \[of Nicaea\] with all the fathers, and even though we have been removed in body, we have still appended our signatures to this document in our own hand.\'

<div align="center"><b>St Mercurius Appears to St Basil with Bloody Spear</b></div>
<div align="center">"Martin Del Rio - Investigations Into Magic Volume 2" Pages 151-151</div>
In 366 the Emperor Julian was killed by the spearhead of an unidentified individual. St Basil had a vision of this before it happened. St Mercurius appeared to him, along with the Blessed Virgin, and as \[the saint was leaving, he was carrying a bloody spear, as St \[John\] of Damascus, relying on Helladius, one of St Basil\'s disciples, reported in his Holy Images 1.

<div align="center"><b>Apostles and Prophets Gather on Julian's Wrongs</b></div>
<div align="center">"Martin Del Rio - Investigations Into Magic Volume 2" Pages 151-151</div>
At the same time, too, someone else, while making his way to the camp, saw, either while he was awake or while he was dreaming, several of the Apostles and prophets gathered together, looking into the wrongs Julian had done to the Church and generally reflecting upon them. Two of their number urged the rest to be of good courage and left and, returning to the company not long afterwards, informed it that the tyrant had been killed. Sozomen tells this story in his \[History of the Church\] Book 6, chapter 2, but leaves out the names of the two men. Nicephorus, however, added that the two were once the famous soldiers and martyrs, Mercurius and Artemius. (See his \[History\] Book 10, chapter 35).

<div align="center"><b>St Febronia Appears Yearly at Midnight</b></div>
<div align="center">"Martin Del Rio - Investigations Into Magic Volume 2" Pages 151-151</div>
St Febronia, virgin and martyr, used to appear every year on her birthday at midnight, during night prayers, to everyone in the choir, occupying the very place where she used to sing the psalms. (\[St Simeon Metaphrastes in Sauer, Volume 3, under 15th June.)

<div align="center"><b>St Antony Sees Soul of St Ammon</b></div>
<div align="center">"Martin Del Rio - Investigations Into Magic Volume 2" Pages 151-151</div>
St Antony saw the soul of St Ammon, accompanied by angels, going to Heaven, (Athanasius, Life of St Antony; Palladius says the same in his Life of Ammon).

<div align="center"><b>Soul of Robber Martyr Appears to St Martin</b></div>
<div align="center">"Martin Del Rio - Investigations Into Magic Volume 2" Pages 151-151</div>
and the soul of the robber who was revered as a martyr rose from the dead \[and appeared to him\], (Sulpicius Severus in his Life of St Martin).

<div align="center"><b>Soul of St Paul the Hermit Appears to St Antony</b></div>
<div align="center">"Martin Del Rio - Investigations Into Magic Volume 2" Pages 151-152</div>
St Athanasius in his Life of \[St\] Antony and St Jerome in his Life of St Martin tell us that the soul of St Paul, the first hermit, appeared to St Antony, borne to Heaven by angels.

<div align="center"><b>Death of St Martin Revealed to Saints</b></div>
<div align="center">"Martin Del Rio - Investigations Into Magic Volume 2" Pages 152-152</div>
The passing of St Martin was shown to St Severinus and St Ambrose while neither of them was present, and he also appeared in order to bring help to those who were preparing to translate his body. He appeared, not just once, elsewhere, as Gregory of Tours says in his books The Miracles of St Martin and The Glory of the Confessors.

<div align="center"><b>St John the Baptist Reveals His Head's Location</b></div>
<div align="center">"Martin Del Rio - Investigations Into Magic Volume 2" Pages 152-152</div>
Herodias had ordered that St John the Baptist\'s head be buried very deep, and many centuries later the saint himself appeared to two monks while they were asleep and showed them where it was; and although the memory of that place was lost and people did not know where \[the head\] was hidden, before Marcian became Emperor St John pointed out, in an extraordinary way, to a monk, Marcellus, the spot where his head was buried. (Prosper and Sigisbert in Sozomen\'s History \[of the Church\] Book 8, chapter 21 and Nicephorus, \[History of the Church\] Book 12, chapter 49).

<div align="center"><b>St Ambrose's Vision of Saints Gervase and Protase</b></div>
<div align="center">"Martin Del Rio - Investigations Into Magic Volume 2" Pages 152-152</div>
St Ambrose found out where the bodies of Saints Gervase and Protase were buried from a vision he had of them, as St Augustine bears witness, (The City of God Book 22, chapter 8 and Confessions Book 9, chapter 7.)

<div align="center"><b>St Ambrose Appears After Death to Holy Men</b></div>
<div align="center">"Martin Del Rio - Investigations Into Magic Volume 2" Pages 152-153</div>
In his biography of St Ambrose, St Paulinus-perhaps \'the Deacon\', not St Paul of Nola-says, \'On the day he died, as it says in a letter which Simplicianus, his successor, a venerable man, received and which was addressed to him from the east, as though \[Ambrose\] were still alive with us-the letter is held permanently in a monastery in Milan-he appeared to certain holy men, praying with them and laying his hands on them. The letter is dated the day on which it was sent, and when we read it, we found it was the day on which \[Ambrose\] died.

<div align="center"><b>St Ambrose Seen Praying in Florence</b></div>
<div align="center">"Martin Del Rio - Investigations Into Magic Volume 2" Pages 153-153</div>
In Tuscany, in the city of Florence, where the holy man Zenobius is now bishop, because he had promised he would visit them quite often, he was frequently seen praying at an altar in the church of Sant\'Ambrogio which he had had built there. (I was told this by the holy priest Zenobius.)

<div align="center"><b>St Ambrose Appears During Siege of Milan</b></div>
<div align="center">"Martin Del Rio - Investigations Into Magic Volume 2" Pages 153-153</div>
In the same house in which he stayed to avoid Eugenius when Rhadagaisus was laying siege to \[Milan\] and the men of the city had already mentally given up hope, he appeared to someone in a vision and promised he would be with them on another day. At this, the citizens\' spirits were raised, and on the second day Stilicho arrived with his army and was victorious over the enemy. (I learned this from Pansophia, a devout woman, mother of the boy Pansophius).

<div align="center"><b>St Ambrose Appears to Mazcezel</b></div>
<div align="center">"Martin Del Rio - Investigations Into Magic Volume 2" Pages 153-153</div>
He appeared to Mazcezel, who was despairing of his own safety and that of the army he was leading against Gildo, in a vision at night. He was holding a walking-stick in his hand and when Mazcezel prostrated himself at the saint\'s feet, the old man struck the earth with the stick he was using to help himself along, (and this was the third time he had appeared to Mazcezel in this guise), and said, \"Here, here, here!\" indicating the spot and giving then man whom he had thought worthy of this visitation to understand that he should realise he would gain victory on the third day in the very place in which he had seen the Lord\'s saintly priest. Thus, he began and ended the war, free from anxiety. (When I was appointed to Milan, I learned all this from what Mazcezel himself had said because in the see in which I now hold an appointment, \[Mazcezel\] had given an account of it to a very large number of priests, and so I thought I could quite safely add to this book what I found out earlier from them.)

<div align="center"><b>Blind Man Healed by Vision of St Ambrose and Companions</b></div>
<div align="center">"Martin Del Rio - Investigations Into Magic Volume 2" Pages 153-153</div>
In Milan we also received, with the greatest reverence, the relics of the martyrs Sisinnius and Alexandrinus who, in my time, after St Ambrose\'s death, gained the crown of martyrdom in the district of Agaunum because of persecutions by the heathen. I found out that a blind man arrived and said he had received his sight on the same day he touched the coffin in which the saints\' relics were being carried. In a vision at night, \[he said\], he had seen a ship approaching the coast, and in it there was a large number of men clad in white. While they were disembarking, he begged one of them to inform him who those men were and was told they were \[St\] Ambrose and his companions. When he heard that name, he prayed he might receive his sight, and the man said to him, \"Go to Milan and present yourself to my brethren who are going to come on\", (and he named the day), \"and you will receive your sight\". The \[blind\] man was from the coast of Dalmatia and kept saying he had never come to the city before until he made his way straight to the saints\' relics. But as soon as he touched them, he began to see\'.

<div align="center"><b>St Eulalia's Spirit Emerges as Dove</b></div>
<div align="center">"Martin Del Rio - Investigations Into Magic Volume 2" Pages 153-153</div>
Here is Prudentius on St Eulalia. \'The virgin, desiring a speedy death, Sought out and drank in the pyre with her mouth From which suddenly a dove sprang forth, Whiter than snow. It was seen To leave the martyr\'s mouth and make for the stars. This was Eulalia\'s spirit \[spiritus\], As white as milk, swift, and innocent.

<div align="center"><b>Vision of St Fructuosus and Martyrs Entering Heaven</b></div>
<div align="center">"Martin Del Rio - Investigations Into Magic Volume 2" Pages 153-153</div>
On St Fructuosus and his friends. \'A servant from the Governor\'s household saw The sky open to let the martyrs in And the illustrious men being carried through the stars. Yes, and he pointed it out to his master\'s little daughter And made her see the sign of her father\'s crimeThat those whom his law-court had killed were now alive in Heaven\'.

<div align="center"><b>Martyrs Instruct on Handling Their Relics</b></div>
<div align="center">"Martin Del Rio - Investigations Into Magic Volume 2" Pages 153-153</div>
When, with devout enthusiasm, each of the brothers later tried to carry off some of the relics for himself, \[Prudentius\] adds, \'But lest they separate the relics, which were to be raised up again And soon exist together with the Lord, By burying them in different places, \[The martyrs\] were seen, clad in snow-white robes. They gave instructions that the dust which would be treated as holy Be given back, mixed together, and enclosed in hollow marble\'.

<div align="center"><b>Ghost Appears to St Germain and Reveals Bodies</b></div>
<div align="center">"Martin Del Rio - Investigations Into Magic Volume 2" Pages 153-154</div>
In chapter 17 of his biography of St Germain d\'Auxerre, the priest Constantinus writes, \'The holy man was staying, undaunted, in a house infested with spectres when suddenly, right in front of a man who was reading a book, there stood a dreadful ghost \[umbra\] which, little by little drew itself erect before his eyes as he looked at it. Showers of stones were being thrown at the walls, too, so the man who had been reading was absolutely terrified and begged the priest to protect him. \[The saint\] immediately jumped up, looked the dreadful figure in the face and, first invoking the name of Christ, ordered it to say who it was and what it was doing there. \[The ghost\] laid aside its frightening lack of reality at once and spoke in a humble voice, like a suppliant, \[saying\] that he and a close friend had committed many crimes and were lying unburied, and that the reason they were disturbing people was that they themselves were unable to be at peace. He asked \[the saint\] to pray to the Lord for them so that they might deserve to receive rest. This made the holy man feel sorry \[for them\] and he told \[the ghost\] to show him where they were lying. Then, carrying a taper in front of him, the ghost led the way ahead and, in the dead of night, pointed out the spot where they had been thrown out among buildings which were in a state of complete ruin. When daylight had returned to the world, \[the saint\] called together people from the neighbourhood and, giving them a good example, applied himself to the work and encouraged them to clear away the old rubbish which had been thrown hurriedly on top of \[the bodies\]. When they had pulled it off with rakes, they found the bodies spreadeagled in a disorderly fashion, their bones still bound tightly with iron \[chains\]. \[The saint\] arranged for a grave to be dug in accordance with the law; the bodies were freed from their chains and clothed in pieces of linen; soil was thrown on top of them and they were buried; a prayer of intercession was said over \[the grave\], and the dead obtained their rest. As a result, after that day the house flourished, many people came to live in it, and there was no sign of \[its former\] horror\'.

<div align="center"><b>Dead Reveal Unburied Bodies to Living</b></div>
<div align="center">"Martin Del Rio - Investigations Into Magic Volume 2" Pages 155-155</div>
When he wrote in chapter 10 that the dead were said to have appeared to the living and that \[the living\] did not know where these people\'s bodies were lying unburied, and that \[the dead\] showed them the places and urged them to give them the burial they had not had, he adds, \'If we answer that these \[reports\] are not true, contrary to what a number of the faithful have written, and contrary to their own senses which confirm that such things have happened to them, people will think us impudent.

<div align="center"><b>Apparitions of Samuel and Moses</b></div>
<div align="center">"Martin Del Rio - Investigations Into Magic Volume 2" Pages 155-155</div>
He also said clearly elsewhere, (chapter 15), in relation to that singular permission, something he did not say about \[God\'s\] usual law which is connected with it. \'Holy Scripture bears witness that apparitions of the dead are sent to the living and confirms this with those of Samuel and Moses\'.

<div align="center"><b>Confessor Felix Appears at Nola</b></div>
<div align="center">"Martin Del Rio - Investigations Into Magic Volume 2" Pages 155-155</div>
and later, in chapter 16, he says that the confessor Felix \[appeared\] when Nola was being attacked by uncouth foreigners, and that he himself knew this not only from the benefits it brought, but also from the looks on people\'s faces, and not just because of unreliable rumours, but because there were reliable witnesses.

<div align="center"><b>Soul of St Jerome Appears to Author of Letter to Cyril</b></div>
<div align="center">"Martin Del Rio - Investigations Into Magic Volume 2" Pages 155-155</div>
The author of the letter to Cyril of Jerusalem, (attributed, albeit falsely, to St Augustine), testifies that the spirits of the dead have taken an interest in what the living do, have assisted those who are still alive, and have been seen in our world. He tells us that St Jerome\'s soul appeared to him at the very time Jerome died and gave him a lot of good advice and learned instruction.

<div align="center"><b>Paesius and Isaias Seen in Heavens by St Pambo</b></div>
<div align="center">"Martin Del Rio - Investigations Into Magic Volume 2" Pages 156-156</div>
In Palladius we read that two brothers, Paesius and Isaias, were seen in the heavens by St Pambo, (in the section on \'Paesius and Isaias\'),

<div align="center"><b>Dead Brother Appears to Father Apollo</b></div>
<div align="center">"Martin Del Rio - Investigations Into Magic Volume 2" Pages 156-156</div>
that his dead brother was seen by Father Apollo, (in the section on \'Apollo\'),

<div align="center"><b>Soul of Anuph Lifted to Heaven</b></div>
<div align="center">"Martin Del Rio - Investigations Into Magic Volume 2" Pages 156-156</div>
and that Anuph had seen the choirs of the blessed and that later on many people saw his soul lifted into Heaven by large numbers of angels and martyrs, (in the section on \'Anuph\').

<div align="center"><b>Angel Appears to Evagrius as Human</b></div>
<div align="center">"Martin Del Rio - Investigations Into Magic Volume 2" Pages 156-156</div>
Palladius was in the habit of explaining things clearly, and distinguishing between the vision of an angel and the vision of a soul, and he added that the angel had taken on human appearance, as you can see in chapter 86 which is about Evagrius the Deacon who was discouraged by the vision of an angel from loving a lecherous woman.

<div align="center"><b>St Procopius Appears in Dream During Storm</b></div>
<div align="center">"Martin Del Rio - Investigations Into Magic Volume 2" Pages 156-156</div>
Marcus of Gaza lived at almost the same time. He tells a story, of which he was an eye-witness, about the delegation of Bishop John of Caesarea and Bishop Porphyrius of Gaza to \[the Emperor\] Arcadius \[seeking permission to demolish the Marneion. In this account along with everything else he describes a very severe storm which God had allowed to rise because of the heretical wickedness of a ship\'s captain. \'We began to call upon \[him, using\] the prayers of St Procopius the Hermit, and when evening had come and the storm had not abated, we remained awake the whole night. Round about morning, however, after a great deal of suffering, the very holy bishops slept a little and, during sleep, my lord Porphyrius saw St Procopius the Hermit who spoke to them. \"Teach the ship\'s captain the catechism\", he said, \"seal him again-because he is a member of Arius\'s hateful sect-make sure he curses Arius and his wicked faith, and this great storm will abate at once\". Then \[Marcus\] adds that this happened and the sea grew calm.

<div align="center"><b>St Paul Helps St John Chrysostom in Writing</b></div>
<div align="center">"Martin Del Rio - Investigations Into Magic Volume 2" Pages 156-156</div>
Proclus of Constantinople saw St Paul helping and giving instructions to St \[John\] Chrysostom as \[John\] was writing his commentaries on St Paul\'s Epistles-this is reported, in writing, by Leo Augustus and \[St Simeon\] Metaphrastes in a Life of St \[John\] Chrysostom-

<div align="center"><b>St Basiliscus Appears to St John Chrysostom</b></div>
<div align="center">"Martin Del Rio - Investigations Into Magic Volume 2" Pages 156-156</div>
and when \[St John\] was coming back from exile, St Basiliscus the Martyr, who suffered some time before in Nicomedia, appeared to him in the church in Comana, saying, \"Take heart, John, because tomorrow we shall be together\'. They say the martyr had also appeared earlier to the church\'s priest and had said, \'Prepare a place for Brother John, because he is about to come \[to Heaven\]\'. Palladius tells the story in his Dialogue⁴⁰ and adds that he confirmed this had happened, because the next day the saintly bishop died and was buried there \[in Comana\].

<div align="center"><b>Mother of God Urges St Cyril to Reconcile with St Chrysostom</b></div>
<div align="center">"Martin Del Rio - Investigations Into Magic Volume 2" Pages 156-156</div>
St Cyril of Alexandria, who was very much at odds with St Chrysostom was told in his sleep by the Mother of God to make his peace with the dead man. (Nicephorus, History \[of the Church\] Book 14, chapter 28, relying on Nicetas.)

<div align="center"><b>Dead Evagrius Appears with Signed Bond to Synesius</b></div>
<div align="center">"Martin Del Rio - Investigations Into Magic Volume 2" Pages 156-157</div>
But an anecdote about Synesius, Bishop of Cyrene, and Evagrius the Philosopher, which Sophronius wrote, (relying on Leontius), in his Spiritual Meadow, chapter 195 is perfectly trustworthy. Synesius was constantly trying to convert \[Evagrius\] to the Christian religion, and \[Evagrius\] kept on objecting to Christian teaching on the resurrection of the body, the reward for good works, especially the hundredfold return after this life for one\'s almsgiving, and used to say he could not but think this was a fairy-tale. But in the end the Bishop, who spared no pains \[to convert him\], persuaded him to become a Christian and baptised him along with his children. \'Not long after he had been baptised, he gave the Bishop three hundred gold pieces to be used for the benefit of the poor, saying, \"Take this gold, distribute it to the poor, and write me a bond in your own hand, saying that Christ will honour it in the next life\". \[Synesius\] took the gold and readily wrote the bond, as Evagrius had asked. The philosopher lived for several years after his baptism, but at length he became mortally ill, and when he was near death he said to his sons, \"When you are making the arrangements for my funeral, put this document in my hands and bury it with me\". After his death, his sons did as he had instructed and buried him with the handwritten bond. On the third day after the burial, he appeared to Bishop Synesius while he was sleeping at night, and said, \"Come to the tomb where I am lying and take your bond, because I have received what I was owed and have had satisfaction; and so that you can be assured of this, I have signed it in my own hand\". Now, the Bishop did not know the bond had been buried with him, but next morning he summoned Evagrius\'s sons and said, \"Tell me, did you put anything in the tomb with your father?\" Thinking he was asking about money, they said, \"Nothing, my lord, except the usual grave clothes. Why do you ask?\" \"Did you, by any chance, bury a document with him?\" The sons still did not know he was talking about a bond but, after thinking about it, said, \"Oh yes, my lord, when he was dying, he did give us some kind of document and said, \"When you bury me, put this document in my hands, but no one is to know about it\". Then the Bishop told them the dream he had had that night and took them, along with some clerics and some of the most important of the citizens, to the philosopher\'s tomb. They opened it and found the philosopher lying there, holding in his hands the bond in the Bishop\'s handwriting. They took the bond from his hands, opened it, and found that the following had recently been added to it in the philosopher\'s handwriting. \"I, Evagrius, a philosopher, greet you, most holy Synesius, my lord Bishop. I have received what I was owed according to what you wrote in your own hand in this paper, have been given satisfaction, and have no further claim against you for the gold I have you and, through you, to Christ, our God and Saviour\", etc.

<div align="center"><b>St Gamaliel Appears to Lucianus Revealing Relics</b></div>
<div align="center">"Martin Del Rio - Investigations Into Magic Volume 2" Pages 157-157</div>
St Gamaliel, St Paul\'s teacher, appeared three times on different nights to Lucianus, a holy man and a priest, who was half awake at the time. (\[This happened\] not during the reign of Constantine-Nicetas makes this mistake in his oration on the martyrdom and discovery of St Stephen-but during that of Honorius and Archidius). He pointed out to him where the relics of his body were, and those of St Stephen, the first martyr, St Nicodemus, and St Abibus. They were found there and brought to the west by Orosius. There exists a letter by Lucianus, which describes this clearly, (see Sauer, Volume 4).

<div align="center"><b>St Gamaliel Appears to Nygetius</b></div>
<div align="center">"Martin Del Rio - Investigations Into Magic Volume 2" Pages 157-157</div>
So that people would have more trust \[in the authenticity\] of this vision, St Gamaliel also appeared at the same time to Nygetius, a monk, and pointed westwards towards the location of the place, as Lucianus himself records.

<div align="center"><b>St Stephen Appears to Several People</b></div>
<div align="center">"Martin Del Rio - Investigations Into Magic Volume 2" Pages 157-157</div>
Evodius is witness that the first martyr himself appeared to several people as well. (See the \[anonymous\] book on the miracles of St Stephen);

<div align="center"><b>Apparition of Micah and Habbakuk</b></div>
<div align="center">"Martin Del Rio - Investigations Into Magic Volume 2" Pages 157-157</div>
and one should read Sozomen, \[History of the Church\] Book 7, last chapter for an apparition of Micah and Habbakuk which happened before the ones I have just mentioned.

<div align="center"><b>Prophet Zacaraiah Appears to Calimerus</b></div>
<div align="center">"Martin Del Rio - Investigations Into Magic Volume 2" Pages 157-157</div>
In Book 9, last chapter, Sozomen says the following about the body of the prophet Zacaraiah, which was discovered not long afterwards. \'Cophar is an estate in the territory of Eleutheropolis in Palestine. This place had an overseer, one Calimerus, a worker on the same estate, who was, to be sure, faithful to his master, but sometimes peevish and awkward and unfair to the neighbouring farmers. But even though he was like this, the prophet revealed himself while he was awake, appearing to him in broad daylight. He pointed out a particular garden and said, \"Please dig there\", etc. and the sacred body was found lying under the designated spot.

<div align="center"><b>Terebon Sees Euthymius at Night</b></div>
<div align="center">"Martin Del Rio - Investigations Into Magic Volume 2" Pages 157-157</div>
Terebon, a Saracen, saw Euthymius at night, although \[Euthymius\] was not in the area and was still alive at the time, and when, later on, \[Euthymius\] had cured him and Terebon had made a journey \[to visit him\], a large number of Saracens embraced the Christian faith. \[This happened\] in the year 420, as Cyril the Monk, an absolutely trustworthy historian has recorded. (See the life of St Euthymius in Sauer, Volume 1, under 20th January).

<div align="center"><b>Virgin Mary, St John Baptist, and St John Evangelist Appear to Cyriacus</b></div>
<div align="center">"Martin Del Rio - Investigations Into Magic Volume 2" Pages 157-157</div>
Round about the year 429 the Blessed Virgin, with St \[John\] the Baptist and St \[John\] the Evangelist, appeared to Father Cyriacus \[the Anchorite\] and said she would not come into his cell. Instead, she stayed outwith the door because, unknown to the Father, there were two books in his cell by Nestorius, an enemy of the Mother of God. (See Sophronius, Spiritual Meadow, chapter 66).

<div align="center"><b>St Paulinus Appears Before Death and Converses with Saints</b></div>
<div align="center">"Martin Del Rio - Investigations Into Magic Volume 2" Pages 157-157</div>
Uranus tells a story about St Paulinus of Nola, (see the life of Paulinus in Sauer, Volume 3, under 22nd June). \[The saint\], he says, appeared to him before he died and St Januarius the martyr and St Martin of Tours had a conversation with him.

<div align="center"><b>Apostles Peter and Apollinaris Appear to Pope Sixtus</b></div>
<div align="center">"Martin Del Rio - Investigations Into Magic Volume 2" Pages 157-157</div>
409 The Apostle Peter and his disciple, St Apollinaris, appeared to and were seen by Pope Sixtus in 433. They suggested that Peter, a very holy and a most eloquent man-truly \'golden of speech\' \[Chrysologus\]-should be made Archbishop of Ravenna. (This comes from the ancient archives of Ravenna in the history of the city by Girolamo Rossi).

<div align="center"><b>St Cyprian Appears to Oppressed Libyans</b></div>
<div align="center">"Martin Del Rio - Investigations Into Magic Volume 2" Pages 158-158</div>
In Book 2 of his Vandalic War, Procopius writes that St Cyprian appeared to the Libyans who had been oppressed and told them to be of good heart, and that in a short time he would be their avenger, and indeed the Vandals were routed two years later.

<div align="center"><b>St Eulalia Appears to Restrain Theodoric</b></div>
<div align="center">"Martin Del Rio - Investigations Into Magic Volume 2" Pages 158-158</div>
In 456, King Theodoric \[II\] conquered the Suevi in Gallaecia \[Galicia\] and marched upon Lusitania \[Portugal\] where he was restrained from destroying the city of Emerita \[Mérida\] by an apparition of the martyr, St Eulalia. (See St Isidore \[of Seville\], History of the Goths, the Vandals, and the Suevi.)

<div align="center"><b>St Peter Corrects Letter on His Tomb</b></div>
<div align="center">"Martin Del Rio - Investigations Into Magic Volume 2" Pages 158-158</div>
In chapter 147 of The Spiritual Meadow, Sophronius \[i.e. Moschus talks about a letter of St Leo to Flavianus about correct faith, and Father Abbot Menas from the same monastery tells us the following story. \'\[The Abbot said\] he had heard Eulogius, the Patriarch of Alexandria, saying, \"When I went to Constantinople, I enjoyed a close friendship with Master Gregory, the Archdeacon of Rome, a remarkable man, and he told me a story about the most holy and blessed Roman Pontiff, Leo. He said that a church in Rome had a written document which said that when \[Leo\] had written a letter to Flavianus, the holy Bishop of Constantinople, against the irreligious Eutyches and Nestorius, he placed it on top of the grave of Peter, the Prince of the Apostles, and then spent time in prayer and vigils and fasts. He begged the chief of the Apostles, \"If, because I am simply a human being, I have written something here I should not have done, \[I ask\] you, to whom our Lord and Saviour Jesus Christ has entrusted both the Church and this See, to put it right\". After four days the Apostle appeared to him and said, \"I have read it and corrected it\". \[Then Leo\] picked up the letter from St Peter\'s tomb, opened it, and found that the Apostle had corrected it in his own hand.

<div align="center"><b>Pope Leo Appears to Theodore in Dream</b></div>
<div align="center">"Martin Del Rio - Investigations Into Magic Volume 2" Pages 158-158</div>
In chapter 148 he goes on to say, \'Theodore, the very holy Bishop of Dorna, which is in Libya, told me the following story. \"When I was chamberlain to holy Pope Eulogius, I dreamed I saw a man whose appearance and aristocratic demeanour inspired awe. He said to me, \"Tell Pope Eulogius I have come\". I said to him, \"Who is it who is telling me to make this announcement?\" He replied, \"I am Leo, the Roman Pontiff\". So, I went in and announced, \"The very holy and blessed Pope Leo, Bishop of the See of Rome, wants to meet you\". When he heard this, Pope Eulogius rose from his seat and ran quickly to meet him. They greeted one another, said a prayer, and then sat down. The distinguished lord Leo said to holy Eulogius, \"Do you know why I have come here to you?\" \"No\", replied Eulogius. \"I have come\", said Leo, \"to thank you for your splendidly correct and proper reply to the letter I sent my brother Flavianus, the Patriarch of Constantinople. You explained my meaning and intention and shut the mouths of the heretics. Please understand, Brother, that you have given your holy labour and exertion not only to me, but also to Peter, supreme head of the Apostles, and to that Truth which is proclaimed to us before all others, Christ our God\". I was reassured by seeing this apparition not merely once, but two and three times, and told the holy Pope Eulogius \[about it\]\'.

<div align="center"><b>St Peter Appears to St Leo Forgiving Sins</b></div>
<div align="center">"Martin Del Rio - Investigations Into Magic Volume 2" Pages 158-158</div>
In chapter 149, Sophronius \[i.e. Moschus\] says that St Peter appeared to the holy Leo on yet another occasion and told him his sins had been forgiven.

<div align="center"><b>Apostles John and Philip Appear to Theodosius</b></div>
<div align="center">"Martin Del Rio - Investigations Into Magic Volume 2" Pages 158-158</div>
Theodoret lived in this century and writes that the Apostles St John and St Philip once appeared to the Emperor Theodosius, (History \[of the Church\] Book 5, chapter 24).

<div align="center"><b>St Barnabas Appears to Anthemius Revealing Relics</b></div>
<div align="center">"Martin Del Rio - Investigations Into Magic Volume 2" Pages 158-158</div>
In the year 485, when Peter the Fuller was trying to bring the Church in Cyprus under his control, the Apostle St Barbabas appeared three times to Bishop Anthemius of Salamis on three successive night and showed him where his body was buried along with a Gospel of St Matthew written in the Evangelist\'s own hand. Both were found. (Alexander the Monk tells the story at length. See Sauret, Volume 3, under 11th June).

<div align="center"><b>Apparition Converts Isidore the Monk</b></div>
<div align="center">"Martin Del Rio - Investigations Into Magic Volume 2" Pages 159-159</div>
Many Severian heretics were converted by various visions-to begin with, for example, Isidore, a monk from Philoxene, \[who was converted\] by an apparition of a man who was damned because he had struck Christ our Lord on the cheek with his hand. (\'Sophronius\' tells the story at length in The Spiritual Meadow, chapter 30.)

<div align="center"><b>Virgin Mary Stops Heretical Cosmiana from Entering Church</b></div>
<div align="center">"Martin Del Rio - Investigations Into Magic Volume 2" Pages 159-159</div>
Then there was Cosmiana, the wife of a patrician Germanus, who was stopped by a visible appearance of the Mother of God and other holy women from entering a church because she was tainted by heresy. (\'Sophronius\', who adds many other examples in chapters 49, 70, 106, 188, and 213.

<div align="center"><b>John the Silent Appears in Dreams to Regina</b></div>
<div align="center">"Martin Del Rio - Investigations Into Magic Volume 2" Pages 159-159</div>
John the Silent appeared in dreams to Regina, a woman from Cappadocia who had the office of deaconess, while he was still alive and living in Lavra, and told her what she needed to do. (Cyril \[of Scythopolis\], a monk, tells the story of this even in his Life of John the Silent. See \[Luigi\] Lippomano, Volume 6.)

<div align="center"><b>St Bartholomew Appears to Anastasius</b></div>
<div align="center">"Martin Del Rio - Investigations Into Magic Volume 2" Pages 159-159</div>
St Bartholomew appeared in Darae to Anastasius and pointed out where his body had been buried and promised to be the city\'s patron and protector. (See Nicephorus, Book 16, chapter 37).

<div align="center"><b>Macedonius's Vision and Warning to Anastasius</b></div>
<div align="center">"Martin Del Rio - Investigations Into Magic Volume 2" Pages 159-159</div>
In the year 515 Macedonius \[II\], the Patriarch of Constantinople, who had been driven into exile by the wicked \[Emperor\] Anastasius, died and \[George\] Cedrenus has this to say about him. \'He was about to be put in his tomb, but before this happened, he raised his right hand and made the sign of the cross over it. In a vision he \[also\] said to Theodorus, one of his close friends, \"Listen to this, and go and tell Anastasius that I, Macedonius, am going to my ancestors in whose faith I have continued steadfastly. In the meantime, I shall keep bothering God until you, too, come and our case receives judgement\".

<div align="center"><b>Visions Warn Elias and Flavianus of Death</b></div>
<div align="center">"Martin Del Rio - Investigations Into Magic Volume 2" Pages 159-159</div>
But because Macedonius died a schismatic, God appointed others to accuse Anastasius, Catholics whom \[the Emperor\] had also sent into exile. God warned both of them in a vision to prepare themselves because they were going to die ten days after Anastasius\'s death and prosecute their case in front of His dread tribunal. These two were Elias, the Patriarch of Jerusalem, and Flavianus, the Patriarch of Antioch. (See Cyril \[of Scythopolis\], Acts of St Sabas in Sauret, Volume 6, under 5th December, and \'Sophronius\', The Spiritual Meadow, chapter 35).

<div align="center"><b>Hermit Sees Theodoric's Soul Thrown into Crater</b></div>
<div align="center">"Martin Del Rio - Investigations Into Magic Volume 2" Pages 159-159</div>
An old hermit in Lipari saw the soul of Theodoric, King of Italy, brought out with its hands bound, and thrown into Vulcan\'s crater. (Pope St Gregory tells the story in Book 4 of his Dialogues, chapter 30.)

<div align="center"><b>Nestorian Monk Sees Heretics in Fires</b></div>
<div align="center">"Martin Del Rio - Investigations Into Magic Volume 2" Pages 159-160</div>
Sometimes it turned out that while he was receiving a vision a person would be brought to a place where souls were being detained, as we are told in the exemplary story of the Nestorian monk whom St Cyriacus entrusted to God\'s care. \'At the ninth hour of the day the brother, who was in his cell, caught sight of someone with a terrifying appearance standing next to him. \"Come and see the truth\", he said, and took hold of \[the monk\] and brought him to a dark, stinking place which was breathing out fire. In those fires \[the monk\] saw Nestorius, Eutyches, Apollinaris, Dioscurus, Severus, Arius, Origen, and a number of others. \"This\", said the apparition, \"is the place which has been prepared for heretics\", etc.

<div align="center"><b>Apostles Appear to Honor Justinian</b></div>
<div align="center">"Martin Del Rio - Investigations Into Magic Volume 2" Pages 159-159</div>
When the Emperor Justinian finished building a church for the Apostles, it is agreed, says Procopius, that \'the Apostles, mindful of his good works, appeared to people in order to honour the King;

<div align="center"><b>Saints Cosmas and Damian Cure Justinian</b></div>
<div align="center">"Martin Del Rio - Investigations Into Magic Volume 2" Pages 159-159</div>
\'More or less at the end of the Golden Horn, on a rather steep, high spot, a church was dedicated some time ago to St Cosmas and St Damian. Here while Justinian while he was lying asleep, seriously ill and already having the look of death on him-indeed his doctors despaired of him and \[treated him as though he were already\] lying among the dead-those saints appeared to him and cured him\'.

<div align="center"><b>St Peter Defends Rome's Walls</b></div>
<div align="center">"Martin Del Rio - Investigations Into Magic Volume 2" Pages 159-159</div>
Procopius also testifies in Book 1 of his Gothic War that a part of Rome\'s defensive walls was defended by the Apostle St Peter when the city was being besieged by the Goths.

<div align="center"><b>St Stephen Intercedes for Metz</b></div>
<div align="center">"Martin Del Rio - Investigations Into Magic Volume 2" Pages 160-160</div>
In Book 2, chapter 6 of his History of the Franks, Gregory \[of Tours\] writes that St Stephen was seen to intercede with the Princes of the Apostles for the city of Metz where his relics were kept;

<div align="center"><b>Virgin Mary Heals Jewish Glass-Worker's Son</b></div>
<div align="center">"Martin Del Rio - Investigations Into Magic Volume 2" Pages 160-160</div>
and in the year 552 the Blessed Virgin showed herself in visible form to the son of a Jewish glass-worker who had been injured after working at the kiln for three days, and healed him. Later on, he and his mother were baptised. (One can look for a perfectly reliable version of what happened in Evagrius Book 4, chapter 35, because Evagrius was alive at the time. Gregory of Tours relies on him in his book, The Glory of the Martyrs, chapter 8, as does Glykas, Annals Part 4.)

<div align="center"><b>St Eutychius Warns Redemptus of End Times</b></div>
<div align="center">"Martin Del Rio - Investigations Into Magic Volume 2" Pages 160-160</div>
While Redemptus, Bishop of Ferentino was keeping watch at the tomb of St Eutychius, the martyr stood near him and said, \'Are you awake, Redemptus?\' Redemptus replied, \'Yes, I am\', and St Eutychius said, \'The end of all flesh is coming\'.

<div align="center"><b>Vision of Chilperic's Punishment to Guntram</b></div>
<div align="center">"Martin Del Rio - Investigations Into Magic Volume 2" Pages 160-160</div>
In about 587, a vision of this kind was given to King Guntram. It was about Chilperic, the Franks\' most wicked tyrant, and King Guntram himself told the story to Gregory of Tours as follows. \'I also saw another vision which gave notice of this man\'s death. He was brought in front of me in chains by three bishops-the first was Tetricus, the second Agricola, and the third Nicetius of Lyons. Two of them were saying, \"Please release him \[from his chains\], give him a sound beating, and allow him to go\". Bishop Tetricus, on the other hand, replied bitterly, \"Don\'t do that! Let him be burned to death for his crimes\". While they were, so to speak, wrangling and exchanging high words at length for a long time, I noticed that a bronze cauldron at some distance from them, which had been placed on top of a fire, was boiling fiercely and, as I wept, they seized the unfortunate Chilperic, broke his arms and legs, and threw him into the cauldron. It was not long before he was so dissolved and melted amid the steaming waters that no trace of him whatever remained there\',

<div align="center"><b>Virgin Mary Appears to Narsetes</b></div>
<div align="center">"Martin Del Rio - Investigations Into Magic Volume 2" Pages 160-160</div>
Evagrius \[345-399} tells us that Narsetes, a eunuch but also a very famous war leader, left a wicked deed unpunished. \'Those who were with Narsetes remembered that while he was placating God with prayers and other acts of devotion, and paying Him the worship due to Him, the holy Virgin appeared to him and distinctly appointed the time at which he should wage war on the enemy, \[saying\] he should not get ready to join battle with the enemy until he had received a sign from Heaven\'.

<div align="center"><b>St Sergius Defends Sergiopolis</b></div>
<div align="center">"Martin Del Rio - Investigations Into Magic Volume 2" Pages 160-160</div>
A little later, while Chosroe was laying siege to Sergiopolis, St Sergius the martyr was seen, with innumerable heavenly defenders, preparing to defend it and running along the walls all over the place. (Nicephorus Book 15, chapter 17, relying on Evagrius Book 4, chapter 27.)

<div align="center"><b>Virgin Mary Turns Against Anatolius and Rouses Faithful</b></div>
<div align="center">"Martin Del Rio - Investigations Into Magic Volume 2" Pages 160-160</div>
While Justinus the Younger was Emperor, first an image of the Mother of God turned its back on Anatolius, an illusionist and an irreligious man, and then the Mother of God herself appeared to several of the faithful and roused them against that wicked man, saying her Son was being troubled by slanders which were coming from Anatolius, (Evagrius Book 15, chapter 18.)

<div align="center"><b>Vision of St Musa and the Virgin Mary</b></div>
<div align="center">"Martin Del Rio - Investigations Into Magic Volume 2" Pages 161-161</div>
One night the blessed Mother of God, the Virgin Mary, appeared to her in a vision and showed her girls of her own age dressed in white garments. Musa wanted to join their company but did not dare do so. The voice of the blessed Virgin Mary asked if she wanted to be with them and live in her service. The girl said, "I do", and immediately received an instruction not to behave in a light-minded and girlish fashion and to refrain from laughing and joking, knowing full well that in thirty days' time she would be entering [the Virgin's] service along with the virgins she had seen.

After seeing this [vision], the girl changed her behaviour entirely and wiped away her girlish light-mindedness with the heavy hand of seriousness. Her parents were astonished at the change in her and when they asked her about it, she told them what the blessed Mother of God had instructed her to do, and on which day she told her she would be entering her service. On the twenty-fifth day she was seized with fever and on the thirtieth, when the hour of her death drew near, she saw the blessed Mother of God coming to her with the girls she had seen in her vision. She began to reply to [the Virgin] who was summoning her and, with her eyes respectfully lowered, she called out in a loud voice, "Look, Lady, I'm coming"; and with these words she gave up her spirit.

<div align="center"><b>Martyrs Appearing to St Probus</b></div>
<div align="center">"Martin Del Rio - Investigations Into Magic Volume 2" Pages 161-161</div>
He speaks about St Probus, the Bishop of Reate. The martyrs St Juvenal and St Eleutherius appeared to him and to a child who was with him. They were wearing white stoles and carried Probus's soul with them into Heaven.

<div align="center"><b>Apparition of Theodoric's Soul</b></div>
<div align="center">"Martin Del Rio - Investigations Into Magic Volume 2" Pages 161-161</div>
Gregory supplies other examples in chapters 11 and 14, and also examples of apparitions of the damned, such as that of Theodoric's soul which was seen to be thrown into Vulcan's pot, [and example] I cited earlier.

<div align="center"><b>Nun Cut in Two</b></div>
<div align="center">"Martin Del Rio - Investigations Into Magic Volume 2" Pages 161-161</div>
Hugo Eterianus confirms this in chapter 7 of his book The Return of Souls, and [St Gregory], Dialogues Book 4, chapter 51 [talks] about a nun who was seen cut in two in front of the altar.

<div align="center"><b>Pascanius the Deacon's Punishment</b></div>
<div align="center">"Martin Del Rio - Investigations Into Magic Volume 2" Pages 161-161</div>
[St Gregory] adds more about souls which were still expiating their sins. 'Pascanius, a deacon, was seen in Rome, standing in the baths and ministering to the bathers as a punishment for the favour he had shown towards a schismatic, as we are told by the man to whom he appeared-Germanus, Bishop of Capua, by whose prayers he was soon set free from his place of punishment.

<div align="center"><b>Bath-House Owner's Post-Death Service</b></div>
<div align="center">"Martin Del Rio - Investigations Into Magic Volume 2" Pages 161-161</div>
He tells a fairly similar story about the soul of the owner of a bath-house. Because of his sins, after he died, he was assigned to the hot rooms of the bath-house and ordered to the unremitting service of those who were going to wash. After he had performed this duty more than once for a priest from Civitavecchia, the priest, as a sign of [fraternal] affection, brought him two pieces of blessed bread, but he, full of sorrow, said, "Why are you giving me these, Father? This bread is holy. I can't eat it. This person you are looking at was once the owner of this place, but after my death I was assigned [to work] here because of my sins. But if you want to help me, offer this bread to Almighty God on my behalf and intercede [for me] on account of my sins. You will know He has heard you when you come here to wash and don't find me at all." With these words he vanished and he, who was a spirit,' etc.

<div align="center"><b>Monk Justus Escapes Punishment</b></div>
<div align="center">"Martin Del Rio - Investigations Into Magic Volume 2" Pages 161-161</div>
In the same chapter, [St Gregory] adds another story about a monk, Justus, who appeared to his brother Copiosus and told him he had escaped punishment because of the offering of the sacrifice of salvation [the Mass]. (Glykas gives a slightly different version in part 4 of his Annals).

<div align="center"><b>Blessed Virgin Appears to St Ildephonsus</b></div>
<div align="center">"Martin Del Rio - Investigations Into Magic Volume 2" Pages 161-162</div>
St Ildephonsus [Hildefuns], Bishop of Toledo, to whom the Blessed Virgin gave a dazzling white garment when she appeared to him with a large number of virgins. (This garment is still preserved today.)

<div align="center"><b>St Leocadia Rises from Grave</b></div>
<div align="center">"Martin Del Rio - Investigations Into Magic Volume 2" Pages 161-162</div>
St Leocadia rose from her grave and appeared to him and the King and the whole clergy and people and seemed to be holding out a large cloth in her hand. In order to test whether this apparition was genuine, the King handed St Ildephonsus a knife and [Ildephonsus] cut off some of the cloth. (This piece of cloth, along with the knife, has been deposited among the treasures of the Church). Julianus Pomerius, a bishop of the same church, testifies to both [stories].

<div align="center"><b>Ebroinus Carried Off by Evil Spirits</b></div>
<div align="center">"Martin Del Rio - Investigations Into Magic Volume 2" Pages 161-162</div>
In 696 a blind man heard Ebroinus being carried off by evil spirits to Vulcan's pot, as Ado of Vienne tells us in his chronicle.

<div align="center"><b>St Suibertus Appears to Sick People</b></div>
<div align="center">"Martin Del Rio - Investigations Into Magic Volume 2" Pages 162-162</div>
St Suibertus who appeared after his death to sick people whom he [then] cured.

<div align="center"><b>Bede's Apparitions in English Church History</b></div>
<div align="center">"Martin Del Rio - Investigations Into Magic Volume 2" Pages 162-162</div>
the Venerable Bede, who makes clear he had the same opinion about apparitions in his History of the English [Church] Book 4, chapters 14 and 25, and Book 5, chapters 14 and 15, and in other passages of the same book and of the Lives of the Saints he wrote.

<div align="center"><b>Virgin Mary Restores St John of Damascus' Hand</b></div>
<div align="center">"Martin Del Rio - Investigations Into Magic Volume 2" Pages 162-162</div>
[At this time] too, lived St John of Damascus. When his hand was cut off on the orders of an iconoclast Emperor, the Blessed Virgin Mother of God restored it, as St John, the Patriarch of Jerusalem, tells us in his biography of him.

<div align="center"><b>St Sabinus Protects Arnulf in Battle</b></div>
<div align="center">"Martin Del Rio - Investigations Into Magic Volume 2" Pages 162-162</div>
At this period lived Paul the Deacon who tells us that Arnulf the Langobard was protected in battle by the martyr, St Sabinus, and by a barbarian [Arnulf] after he had seen and recognised a painting of the martyr.

<div align="center"><b>Translation of St Euphemia's Relics</b></div>
<div align="center">"Martin Del Rio - Investigations Into Magic Volume 2" Pages 162-163</div>
What Bishop Constantine says is entirely worthy of astonishment. He was an eyewitness of the translation of the relics of St Euphemia the Martyr, (see [Luigi] Lippomano, Volume 6). Blinded by the splendour of her miracles, Leo Isauricus secretly removed the martyr's relics and put dry bones in their place, and threw the genuine relics, along with their reliquary, into the sea waves. Some sailors came upon the reliquary but did not know what it was and, thinking some kind of treasure had been put in it, they took it and opened it and, drenched in the sweet scent which breathed miraculously from it, realised these were holy relics, and although they remained ignorant of whose [relics] they were, that same night they saw lights and candles and men shining wonderfully white and praising God.

'When they landed in Levinum and had gone to sleep, during their repose they saw the martyr Glyceria meet the virgin Euphemia, embrace her, exchange a kiss with her, and congratulate her on her arrival. Then they realised whose the relics were. Three times they set sail from Levinum, and three times they were driven back by contrary winds. Finally, Euphemia stood in front of them in their dreams and told them who she was. She said she wanted to stay there because of what had happened to her after she had been thrown into the sea by the irreligious Leo.'

<div align="center"><b>Dream of Leo the Armenian's Mother</b></div>
<div align="center">"Martin Del Rio - Investigations Into Magic Volume 2" Pages 163-163</div>
A little later Zonaras writes of Leo the Armenian as follows. 'These things disturbed the Emperor and a dream his mother had also frightened him. She thought she was in the Church of the Mother of God in Blachernia and saw a lady accompanied by young people who were wearing white garments. The floor of the church was awash with blood, and she heard the lady giving instructions that a dish filled with that blood was to be given to the Emperor's mother. When the Emperor's mother objected, the lady said, "But your son fills those who venerate me with blood and does not realise that he is moving God and my Son to anger". (These words make it clear that the lady was the Blessed Virgin.)

<div align="center"><b>St Tharasius Appears in Dream</b></div>
<div align="center">"Martin Del Rio - Investigations Into Magic Volume 2" Pages 163-163</div>
Zonaras adds, 'St Tharasius, too, was now translated from this wretched life. Someone saw him, in sleep, calling upon a certain Michael and urging him to seize hold of Leo and kill him'; and actually Michael Balbus [Emperor Michael II] did kill him not long after in 787.

<div align="center"><b>St Andrew Appears to Aonghus</b></div>
<div align="center">"Martin Del Rio - Investigations Into Magic Volume 2" Pages 163-163</div>
St Andrew the Apostle appeared to Aonghus, King of the Picts, and promised him victory, a promise he fulfilled. While [the King] was fighting, a red saltire appeared in the sky.

<div align="center"><b>Apparition of St Gertrude</b></div>
<div align="center">"Martin Del Rio - Investigations Into Magic Volume 2" Pages 163-163</div>
At this time lived St Gertrude, an apparition of whom is mentioned by Louis of Blois more than once in his Spiritual Instruction.

<div align="center"><b>St James Appears to Charlemagne</b></div>
<div align="center">"Martin Del Rio - Investigations Into Magic Volume 2" Pages 163-163</div>
Not long afterwards the Roman Empire was transferred to Charlemagne and St James, son of Zebedee, appeared to him and urged him to seize the kingdoms of Spain from Saracen control, as a number of more recent writers have recorded.

<div align="center"><b>St James Appears to Kings of Spain</b></div>
<div align="center">"Martin Del Rio - Investigations Into Magic Volume 2" Pages 163-163</div>
Apparitions of St James to Kings of Spain were quite reliably witnessed during this and the following centuries. He promised he would bring them help in battle and was seen to put the enemy to flight during the fighting. The Moors, too, said they saw him and our men boasted of it.

<div align="center"><b>St James Aids Ramirez in Battle</b></div>
<div align="center">"Martin Del Rio - Investigations Into Magic Volume 2" Pages 163-164</div>
In that year Ramirez, King of Spain, fought very bravely for a whole day with a very large number of Saracens and then, under cover of night, retreated with a tiny band of his own men to a particular hill. While the King was staying awake and praying to God, the saint stood near him and told everyone to cleanse themselves by confession and receive the eucharist, and they would win the battle. In the morning everyone to a man complied with the saint's instructions, and then they picked up the standards and cut sixty thousand of the enemy to pieces. The Apostle was seen mounted on a white horse during this battle, waving a white flag with a distinctive transverse red cross on it.

<div align="center"><b>St Maurilius Appears to Numonis</b></div>
<div align="center">"Martin Del Rio - Investigations Into Magic Volume 2" Pages 164-164</div>
During the reign of Charles the Bald, King of France, someone called Numonis, a usurper of the Church's goods, saw and felt St Maurilius who appeared to him, upbraided him loudly, and struck his head with his holy crozier. Nor was the vision in vain. Numonis died a little later.

<div align="center"><b>Pandulf's Torments</b></div>
<div align="center">"Martin Del Rio - Investigations Into Magic Volume 2" Pages 164-164</div>
Likewise, one reads in Book 2, chapter 62 of the Chronicles of [Monte] Cassino that a child caught sight of Pandulf, Prince of Capua, bound with iron restraints, dropped into a muddy, stinking lake right up to his throat. He was being dropped into the deep [water] and immediately hauled out again with ropes by two jet-black spirits [spiritibus]. The child asked him why this was happening, and he replied, 'Because I stole a golden chalice from St Benedict's monastery and failed to put it back [before] I was in the throes of death'. Chapter 84 [says] a hermit saw Aethiopians, who said they were evil spirits, laden with straw and preparing a pyre for that same Pandulf: and it was found he had died at that very hour.

<div align="center"><b>Ludger's Dream of St Lebuinus</b></div>
<div align="center">"Martin Del Rio - Investigations Into Magic Volume 2" Pages 164-164</div>
While Ludger was looking in vain for the body of St Lebuinus, at length in sleep he had a notion that the very holy priest of Christ was talking to him and telling him where he was buried: and parts of his body were discovered in the place the spirit [spiritus] indicated.

<div align="center"><b>Apostles Peter and Paul in Battle Against Saracens</b></div>
<div align="center">"Martin Del Rio - Investigations Into Magic Volume 2" Pages 164-164</div>
When [Pope] John X sent an army into Apulia against the Saracens, the Apostles St Peter and St Paul were seen during the battle, procuring a very great victory for the Christians.

<div align="center"><b>St Theodore Aids Emperor John Zimisca</b></div>
<div align="center">"Martin Del Rio - Investigations Into Magic Volume 2" Pages 164-164</div>
St Theodore the Martyr, by command of the Blessed Virgin, was seen by many and brought help to Emperor John Zimisca while he was fighting the Russians.

<div align="center"><b>St James Aids Fernán González</b></div>
<div align="center">"Martin Del Rio - Investigations Into Magic Volume 2" Pages 164-164</div>
In the year 914, Fernán González, Count of Castile, an illustrious proof of both good and bad fortune, a man noble in both word and deed, relying upon God's counsel overthrew Al-Mansur's enormous force with only three hundred men. Sixteen years later he also fought an unbelievable number of Arabs for three continuous days with one thousand five hundred infantry and four hundred and fifty cavalry beneath his standards, and on the final day St James was seen to be with them in the fighting. Innumerable men were slaughtered, but [González] was triumphant.

<div align="center"><b>St Andrew's Vision to Godfrey of Bouillon</b></div>
<div align="center">"Martin Del Rio - Investigations Into Magic Volume 2" Pages 165-165</div>
In this century there was holy war under the leadership of Godfrey of Bouillon. During the expedition to Antioch our men almost died of famine and nearly ran out of horses but were strengthened by a vision and the admonitions of St Andrew who also showed them the Lord's holy lance. They obtained more than one victory and during the battle with Kerbogha, too, lines of white horses appeared, which put the Persians to flight.

<div align="center"><b>Bishop Adhemar Leads Soldiers</b></div>
<div align="center">"Martin Del Rio - Investigations Into Magic Volume 2" Pages 165-165</div>
During this same war, when the Christians captured the holy city, Bishop Adhemar, who had died long before, was seen leading the soldiers, scaling the walls, and encouraging his men to follow.

<div align="center"><b>Christ and Saints Appear to Emperor Henry II</b></div>
<div align="center">"Martin Del Rio - Investigations Into Magic Volume 2" Pages 165-165</div>
Shortly before that, Christ our Lord, together with the Blessed Virgin, St Peter, St John, St Stephen, St Martin, and many other angels besides, showed Himself to the Emperor Henry II at night while the Emperor was keeping vigil in a church in Rome.

<div align="center"><b>St Dunstan's Dead Friend Predicts Events</b></div>
<div align="center">"Martin Del Rio - Investigations Into Magic Volume 2" Pages 165-165</div>
At that time one of St Dunstan's dead friends appeared to the saint and predicted that many things were going to happen, which did indeed take place.

<div align="center"><b>St Odilo Appears After Death</b></div>
<div align="center">"Martin Del Rio - Investigations Into Magic Volume 2" Pages 165-165</div>
St Odilo, Abbot of Cluny, was seen by friends more than once after his death.

<div align="center"><b>Two Noble Faventi Appear from Hell</b></div>
<div align="center">"Martin Del Rio - Investigations Into Magic Volume 2" Pages 165-165</div>
Peter Damian, a very learned and most eloquent man, flourished at this time and lived into the next century. ... His works-and there are many of them-are filled with various kinds of apparition, such as those of the two noble Faventi who appeared out of Hell.

<div align="center"><b>Souls Appear as Small Birds</b></div>
<div align="center">"Martin Del Rio - Investigations Into Magic Volume 2" Pages 165-165</div>
or the souls which appeared in the form of small birds.

<div align="center"><b>Benedict VIII on Black Horse</b></div>
<div align="center">"Martin Del Rio - Investigations Into Magic Volume 2" Pages 165-165</div>
or the soul of Benedict VIII who appeared, sitting on a black horse, to the Bishop of Capua.

<div align="center"><b>Apparition of Benedict IX</b></div>
<div align="center">"Martin Del Rio - Investigations Into Magic Volume 2" Pages 165-165</div>
Not only Damian (chapter 4), but also Martin of Poland, St Antoninus, and [Bartolommeo] Platina recorded an apparition of Benedict IX.

<div align="center"><b>St Andrew and St Gregory Flog Apostate Monk</b></div>
<div align="center">"Martin Del Rio - Investigations Into Magic Volume 2" Pages 165-165</div>
and Damian (chapter 11) one of St Andrew and St Gregory flogging an apostate monk.

<div align="center"><b>Foundation of the Carthusians Apparition</b></div>
<div align="center">"Martin Del Rio - Investigations Into Magic Volume 2" Pages 165-165</div>
It is worth noting the story of the foundation of the Carthusians. The occasion is well known and in the public domain. On the first, second, and third day during vigils for the dead. An apparition [was seen] while they were singing the verse 'Reply to me' [Job 13.22].
