The dead man raised his head three times and called out that, by God's righteous decision, he had been accused, he had been judged, and he had been sentenced.

<div align="center"><b>Predecessors Appear to St Hanno</b></div>
<div align="center">"Martin Del Rio - Investigations Into Magic Volume 2" Pages 165-165</div>
In this century lived Bishop St Hanno of Köln and Bishop St Benno of Meissen. St Hanno's predecessors as bishop appeared to him, pointed out a stain on his garment, and in this notable fashion impressed on him that he should entirely get rid of his bitterness of mind towards those who had unjustly done him wrong, and forget about it.

<div align="center"><b>St Benno Appears to Margrave</b></div>
<div align="center">"Martin Del Rio - Investigations Into Magic Volume 2" Pages 165-165</div>
Of St Benno it is recorded that after his death he appeared in sleep to the Margrave of Meissen and dug out one of his eyes because he had inflicted damage on the Church.

<div align="center"><b>Christ Encourages Alfonso of Portugal</b></div>
<div align="center">"Martin Del Rio - Investigations Into Magic Volume 2" Pages 166-166</div>
Notice if you will that in 1112 or rather 1139 Alfonso, King of Portugal, was about to join battle with five Saracen kings when he was encouraged, during his sleep, by Christ to be of good heart and to use a standard on which was embroidered an image of the Five Wounds during the battle. He gained a memorable victory, and this was the origin of the royal arms of Portugal.

<div align="center"><b>St Isidore Appears to Alfonso of Castile</b></div>
<div align="center">"Martin Del Rio - Investigations Into Magic Volume 2" Pages 166-166</div>
Fourteen years later Alfonso, King of Castile, was besieging Baéza. St Isidore appeared to him and encouraged him to join battle, and there has scarcely been a more famous victory than this.

<div align="center"><b>Tiny Child in Cremona Speaks</b></div>
<div align="center">"Martin Del Rio - Investigations Into Magic Volume 2" Pages 166-166</div>
In the year 1117, along with a very large number of other extraordinary events which were agitating Italy, 'In Cremona a tiny child was lying in its cradle, wrapped up in its bed-clothes. Contrary to what happens naturally, it opened its mouth and began to speak, interrupting its mother while she was seeing to his elder brother's physical needs and preparing food for him because he had been crying and asking for something to eat. [The child] told her he had seen Mary, the Mother of God, standing in front of Christ's judgement-seat, supplicating Him with her most earnest prayers because of the judgement which He had laid upon the world because of its sins. After this, [the child] did not speak again until it was the appropriate time in the course of human nature for it to do so'.

<div align="center"><b>Pope Benedict X Appears</b></div>
<div align="center">"Martin Del Rio - Investigations Into Magic Volume 2" Pages 166-166</div>
An apparition of Pope Benedict X appeared first of all to João [Peculiar], Bishop of Porto, in which [the Pope] confessed he had been saved from the danger of everlasting death by the prayers of Abbot Odilo. He then appeared to Edelbert and also confessed he had been set free from the pains of Purgatory.

<div align="center"><b>St Norbert Appears to Household</b></div>
<div align="center">"Martin Del Rio - Investigations Into Magic Volume 2" Pages 166-166</div>
St Norbert, too, appeared after his death to his household.

<div align="center"><b>St Bernard's Uncle Gualdric Appears</b></div>
<div align="center">"Martin Del Rio - Investigations Into Magic Volume 2" Pages 166-166</div>
One night, St Bernard saw his uncle Gualdric who had died several days earlier.

'How are you?' he asked. 'I'm fine', replied his uncle. Then Bernard asked what was the reason he was bellowing in agony [just before he died], and why his body was being wracked in a dreadful manner. 'At that very moment', said Gualdric, 'two vile spirits [spiritus] were doing their best to hurl me into a very deep pit, but St Peter came to my aid and I escaped'.

<div align="center"><b>Blessed Virgin Appears to Rupert of Deutz</b></div>
<div align="center">"Martin Del Rio - Investigations Into Magic Volume 2" Pages 166-166</div>
Rupert tells us that the Blessed Virgin made herself visible to him and urged him to write.

<div align="center"><b>Apparitions to Mary of Egypt, Theophilus, and Children of Israel</b></div>
<div align="center">"Martin Del Rio - Investigations Into Magic Volume 2" Pages 166-166</div>
and in chapter 1 of his Sign of Mary, Honoré mentions Mary of Egypt to whom the Mother of God appeared and drew to repentance, and Theophilus whom she snatched from slavery to the Devil, and the children of Israel whom she protected in the furnace.

<div align="center"><b>St Isidore Transforms St Martin</b></div>
<div align="center">"Martin Del Rio - Investigations Into Magic Volume 2" Pages 166-166</div>
St Martin, a priest and canon regular, lived at this time in León where he wrote various books. He was suddenly transformed from an uneducated man with no Latin to a very good scholar by St Isidore, in whose monastery he was living. [St Isidore] appeared to him while he was asleep and offered him a book which he read through eagerly from beginning to end.

<div align="center"><b>St James and St Isidore Aid in Battle</b></div>
<div align="center">"Martin Del Rio - Investigations Into Magic Volume 2" Pages 167-167</div>
[Juan de Mariana, (Book 12, chapter 15), [Esteban de Garibay y] Zamalloa, and other writers on the annals of the history of Spain tell us that St James appeared to Alfonso, King of León, at Mérida, and that St Isidore appeared to others at Zamora at the same time and brought them help while they were fighting.

<div align="center"><b>Elderly Ecclesiastic's Bier Moves</b></div>
<div align="center">"Martin Del Rio - Investigations Into Magic Volume 2" Pages 167-167</div>
I shall add at least some of the more notable examples from these last centuries, because my opponents make little of more recent [examples]. First, therefore-and I cannot be sure of the century-I shall relate here what Glykas [says] in part 4 of his Annals. 'In the history of the Church by the historian Philo, one finds that at a particular moment during the ancient persecutions, a bishop banned a rather elderly ecclesiastic from [holding] church services. But when that elderly man went elsewhere to do something he had to do, it happened he was seized by natives and gave witness in his own person to the truth. In consequence, a church was founded on the spot and the ceremonies of consecration carried out. When the Bishop started to pronounce the words, "Peace be to everyone", the bier went out the church, and this happened not once, but two or three times. From there the elderly man addressed the Bishop from the sleep [of death]. "I'm going", he said, "but please intercede for me with my bishop [and ask] him to come here and release me from my bonds, because he excluded me from my sacred office and so I can't be present with you at religious services. I have obtained the crown of my witnessing, but I have not yet seen God's face. But if [the Bishop] comes here and does not release me, no one else will be able to do so". Accordingly, when [his Bishop] complied with these [requests], the bier ceased leaving the church.'

<div align="center"><b>Udo Bishop of Magdeburg's Judgment</b></div>
<div align="center">"Martin Del Rio - Investigations Into Magic Volume 2" Pages 167-168</div>
This is an appropriate place to record the revenge taken by divine providence upon a wicked bishop. It happened during the tenth century but was omitted from my earlier account. 'When Udo, Bishop of Magdeburg, was not moved even by signs and prophetic voices to refrain from lewd behaviour, the clergy asked God either to amend or to remove him. One of their number, Canon Frederik, was praying after this fashion in the Cathedral of St Maurice at night, when he noticed that all the lights in the church were extinguished by a rather strong gust of wind, and not long afterwards that two youths carrying two candelabra with lighted candles came in, followed closely by Christ, His mother, and the Apostles. They summoned the holy people whose bodies were lying at rest in the church, and [St] Maurice was seen to come along with them. In a long, serious speech he laid an accusation against Bishop Udo and not long after that Christ ordered the two [youths] to fetch him, stripped of his clothes. He passed sentence against him, but the bishop put up a fight and one of the two who were bringing him struck him a violent blow in the midst of his kidneys, [whereupon], into a chalice which had been placed on the altar, the Bishop vomited up the Host of Christ which he had taken in communion the previous day. Then Udo was struck down by an axe and the vision and everyone in it vanished. Frederik was therefore absolutely terrified when he went up to the altar, looked in the chalice, [and saw] that it contained the Host of Christ and that the Bishop was lying dead on the ground. He woke the other clergy and they removed the Bishop's body and buried it in a field'.

<div align="center"><b>Galeazzo Sforza's Spirit Warns Merchants</b></div>
<div align="center">"Martin Del Rio - Investigations Into Magic Volume 2" Pages 168-168</div>
'Two wealthy merchants who came from not undistinguished families were making their way to France via the Mont Genèvre Pass when they met a man of larger than human appearance and received an instruction from him which went as follows. "Speak to my brother Lodovico Sforza and give him this letter on my behalf". They were rendered speechless and wondered who he was. He told them he was Galeazzo Sforza, and not long afterwards vanished from their eyes. They hastily returned to Milan and from there went to Vigevano where [Ludovico] 'The Moor' was staying and delivered the Duke's letter whose contents were as follows.

"Oh, oh, oh, Ludovico! Watch out! The Venetians and the French are about to come and destroy you and overthrow your House, but if you give me three thousand gold pieces, I shall help you to mollify the spirits [spiritibus] and get them to avert your hapless fate: and I promise this will be the result, provided you agree and don't oppose me. Goodbye", signed, "The spirit of your brother, Galeazzo".

Some people may laugh at this as an invention, but not long afterwards the prince was ejected from his principality by Louis XII, King of France, and taken into captivity'.

<div align="center"><b>Lodovico's Father Appears to Secretary</b></div>
<div align="center">"Martin Del Rio - Investigations Into Magic Volume 2" Pages 168-169</div>
'Not long after he died,' (says [Marc Antonio] Sabellico), 'Lodovico's father, the lord of Imola, appeared to a secretary who was being sent to Ferrara by his son, Lodovico. [He appeared] while the man was on his way and told him to tell his son to meet him there the next day because he had something of great importance to say to him. When Lodovico heard this, he sent someone else in his place because he did not believe it and because he was afraid it was a trap. The same ghost [umbra] who had appeared before met the man and was deeply pained that his son had not come, because he said he had a good many things to tell him. On this occasion, however, he wanted to say just this-that after twenty-two years and one month had passed, (and he added a specific day), Lodovico would lose the control of the city which he now enjoyed; and when the time predicted by the ghost arrived, even though great care had been taken on the very night his father's spirit [manes] had cast suspicion, the confederate army of Duke Filippo of Milan got as far as the walls, since most of the ditches were frozen solid, set up ladders, and captured the city along with its prince,'

<div align="center"><b>Spirit of Ferdinand King of Naples Appears</b></div>
<div align="center">"Martin Del Rio - Investigations Into Magic Volume 2" Pages 168-169</div>
In Book 1 of his History [of Italy], Francesco Guicciardini says that a rumour spread around that the spirit of Ferdinand, King of Naples, appeared on three different nights to Jacopo, a surgeon [in the household] of his son King Alfonso, and ordered him, in mild and gentle language at first, but later with threats and reproaches, to tell Alfonso, in the words he was actually using, that there was no reason for him to flatter himself with the worthless hope that he could keep French power in check, because it had been decided and determined by the law of Fate that the House of Aragon was to be shaken by an endless number of misfortunes and, in the end, deprived of its kingdom.

Guicciardini, however, does add, 'One is, however, at liberty not to disparage such things entirely', and he added it, not in relation to the apparition, but to the trustworthiness of the prediction. He was quite right to do so, because we see it was not true.

<div align="center"><b>Giovanni Pico's Ghost to Savonarola</b></div>
<div align="center">"Martin Del Rio - Investigations Into Magic Volume 2" Pages 169-169</div>
Count Gianfrancesco Pico della Mirandola writes in his biography of his uncle, Giovanni Pico, that not long after his death, Giovanni's ghost [spectrum] appeared to Girolamo Savonarola and told him he was being tortured by the pains of atonement because he had not multiplied, with sufficient diligence and fertile results, the talent of learning and cleverness God had credited to him, and because he had not made a proper return on God's inward suggestions and inspirations which kept urging him not to break off the honourable labours he had begun and which he had told himself mentally to undertake in earnest and bring to a conclusion. Not long afterwards, Girolamo told people about this in one of his public addresses and commended Pico to everyone's prayers.

<div align="center"><b>Marsilio Ficino Appears to Michele Mercati</b></div>
<div align="center">"Martin Del Rio - Investigations Into Magic Volume 2" Pages 169-169</div>
Cesare Baronio testifies of the elder Michele Mercati that Michele and Marsilio [Ficino] were very close friends because they were deeply interested in the same things and were closely bound together by [their belonging to] the School of Plato. One day, however, it happened 'that as usual [they were discussing] Plato's opinion on which part of a human being survives after death and, not without consternation, they came to the conclusion that [his arguments] were unstable and needed to be propped up by the mysteries of the Christian faith. (A learned letter from Marsilio to Michele Mercati about the immortality of the spirit and God, [with a reference] to this deduction still exists).

But when they had argued their differences for quite a long time, they brought their discussion to an end and closed it by agreeing to make a pact that whichever one of them should die first would, if he were permitted, tell the other about his state in the next life. Having made this agreement, they both swore their oath and then went their separate ways. After only a brief lapse of time it happened that Michele the elder was engaged in philosophical studies in the middle of the morning when he suddenly began to hear the racket made by a horse galloping at speed. It stopped at his door and Marsilio's voice cried out, "Michele, Michele, it's true, it's true!" Surprised by his friend Marsilio's voive, Michele got up, opened the window, and saw the man he had heard riding away again, mounted on a white horse. He shouted after the white figure, calling him by name, "Marsilio, Marsilio!" and pursuing him with his eyes. But he vanished from them. Astounded by this strange event and feeling anxious about Marsilio, Michele went and made careful inquiries-Marsilio was living in Florence at the time of his death-and found out that Marsilio had died at the very time he had heard and seen him'.

<div align="center"><b>Pedro de Paz Appears in Siege of Antwerp</b></div>
<div align="center">"Martin Del Rio - Investigations Into Magic Volume 2" Pages 169-170</div>
[But] I do include one [example of an apparition] which one can rely on because of the evidence of many perfectly serious soldiers who solemnly swore they had seen it. Some years ago, when Alessandro Farnese was conducting his remarkable siege of Antwerp, in order to help the besieged the Dutch and English made a sally, and so did the besieged at the same time with a view to keeping the enemy occupied. They fought very fiercely, seized, and took possession of the royal army's earthwork, and appeared to be free from danger. At that moment, the more distinguished of the King's soldiers started to see Pedro de Paz near the earth-work-a Spanish commander and a man very much praised for his military qualities and the attention to duty which marked him out. He had died a few months earlier and on this occasion was seen fully armed as he used to be when leading his regiment. He signalled to his former soldiers and gave them the order to follow him. The front rank pointed him out to the second, the second to the third, and the third to those behind them. They all saw the same thing and, full of astonishment, plucked up their spirits and followed the leader they knew so well. He went in front of them and led them straight towards the enemy, and the fighting started. The Dutch, however, were driven back to their ships, leaving the earthwork to the King's troops, and at that moment the town, which was very well fortified, lost its hope of victory and of defending itself.

<div align="center"><b>Notary's Corpse Rises</b></div>
<div align="center">"Martin Del Rio - Investigations Into Magic Volume 2" Pages 170-170</div>
A quite dreadful thing to read is something which happened in Pavia earlier this year (1601) in April, in the diocese of a small town called Corretto. A notary's funeral was taking place in the church, when suddenly the corpse raised himself from his bier, turned to one of his relatives who was attending the funeral, and told him to hurry to his house, and to take a number of [hand-]written documents which were there and put them straight back in a holy place. Because he had concealed them, the dead man [said], God had justly sentenced him to the torments of Hell, having said which, he laid his head down as before. God permitted this so that mortals might realise what serious penalties await treacherous clerks of this kind who embezzle the legacies of people who are devout.

<div align="center"><b>Katarina's Damnation and Hauntings</b></div>
<div align="center">"Martin Del Rio - Investigations Into Magic Volume 2" Pages 170-172</div>
I shall also write down a second anecdote, one worthier of being remembered, about an apparition [spectri]-I do not know whether it was of an evil spirit or a damned soul-which I did not recall I had read. I hope the pleasure and use [the reader will gain] from reading it will overcome its length. It has been taken from a letter from Peru, dated 1590, and is told in the actual words either of Francesco Benci or Gaspar Spitilli.

'An extraordinary thing, well worthy thinking about, happened to this same Fr Samaniego during the mission', (the one to Itata), 'and the inhabitants of the city where it took place have known nothing like the one which has happened to him. It is confirmed by so many testimonies, too, that there is no room left for doubt. It was experienced by people who saw it with their own eyes and heard it. This event, unfortunate in its outcome, was allowed [to happen] -and one can believe this about similar things which people have confessed have happenedso that a population newly converted could learn that the sacrament of penance, in which one finds it difficult [to confess] sins which are not inconsiderable, must be treated with good faith and integrity. Consequently, the Indian woman who, everyone could see, was violating the strict rule that confession must be complete, was punished and chastised in sight of everyone, so that the salvation of many souls could be procured by the downfall of one. What happened was this.

In the house of a distinguished lady of this locality lived a young girl aged about sixteen, who had been captured during war and baptised. She was called Katarina. As she grew older, so did her lack of self-restraint and dissolute behaviour, even though she was not infrequently rebuked and punished by her mistress. The girl came to such a pitch of wickedness that she began secretly to frequent [the company of certain profligate individuals. Yet she did not fail to go to confession, although she kept her mouth shut about this sin in case people would think she was a little tart, or someone whose morals were past recovery. On 1st August 1590 she fell ill and sent for a priest, to whom she laid bare her soul's offences. She did not do so entirely, however. The priest came and went nine times during her illness, but she would laugh scornfully [and say] something like this to the other servants who were there. "That other sort of thing I was doing-it wasn't what I'd confess as one of my sins", and she used such shameful, disgraceful language as she said it that all the other servants were offended and reported it, word for word, to their mistress. She quite rightly shouted at Katarina, but then changed her expression and tone and asked in a friendly way what were those [sins] she was unwilling to confess to the Father. Katarina had no problem in telling her, and said that every time she sent for the Father during her illness so that she could cleanse herself in confession, someone looking like an Aethiopian stood on her left and kept telling her not to confess because those [particular] sins were very slight and of no importance, and if she confessed them the Father would be able to think she was more dissolute [than she was]. But on her right St Mary Magdalene appeared and urged her to purge herself frankly of whatever it was.

The Father came again, and the lady acquainted him with everything that had happened, and he tried in every possible way to get her to make a full atonement for [the benefit of her soul. He did so, however, in vain. The more he exhorted, the more stubborn she became-to the extent that she was unwilling to pronounce the word "Jesus". On another occasion, too, they offered her a holy picture of the crucifixion so that she could contemplate it and reflect that Christ was nailed to the cross and died on the cross for us. But with the greatest disdain and emotional agitation she replied, "I already know that. What do you want me to do about it?" Her mistress said to her, "We want you to turn to Christ so that if you acknowledge [the sins you have committed, He can forgive them". Katarina answered, "Please stop bothering me", and when her mistress had gone away, she started to talk in a sing-song voice about her loves and her shameful behaviour. She kept this up for several days, [talking about] the things she did and said, until one night her mistress came along with [some of the female servants, and Katarina burst out, "I'm on the rack and in agony because I have profaned confession; and from that very moment until midnight her whole body became stiff.

They thought she had died and began to think about digging her grave and giving her a funeral. But she came to, and the priest was sent for. She, however, made no change at all from the way she had usually spoken before. Three hours later, not long before she died, the servants urged her to take a cross and a holy candle in her hand and invoke the name of Jesus. But she replied, "Who is that Jesus? I don't know the name of Jesus", and she turned back to the end of the bed, sat on it, and was heard having a conversation with someone they could not see. Another female servant who was lying sick in the same room earnestly begged her mistress to have her moved to another bedroom because, she said, she could see a number of black hobgoblins [larvas] and she was absolutely terrified of them. On the night Katarina died, the whole house was pervaded by such a foetid stench of corruption that the corpse had to be put in a place open to the air.

The lady's brother was dragged out of bed by his arm; a female servant was hit on the shoulder by a small stone and carried the marks of her injury for several days; stones rained against a wall, and a horse which in other respects was perfectly tame ran hither and thither and went mad all night long; and dogs did the same, running about and barking. After the body had been buried, one of the female servants went into the room in which Katarina had lain ill, and even though she saw no one, she had the experience of having a dish, which had been put on the wooden floor, being thrown at her. The greater part of the town saw a very large number of slates and roof-tiles hurled about, with a great deal of crashing and noise, up to a distance of two miles-although there is not any slate or roof-tile on the big house because, for the most part, all this city's buildings are roofed with palm leaf. Another female slave was dragged by the foot a very long way while many people looked on, and yet they could not see who was dragging her.

On 7th October, when a female servant went into the wardrobe to fetch a dress for herself, she saw Katarina slowly rising to her feet to seize hold of a plate, and when she ran away, Katarina threw the plate at the wall so violently that it broke into a thousand pieces. Next day a paper crucifix was pinned to the wardrobe, but it was torn down from the wall in front of everyone's eyes and ripped into three pieces. On the same day, while the lady was having her dinner in the garden, a slate was thrown into the middle of her plate, all the food fell on the ground, and her four-year old son started shouting, "Mummy, Mummy! Katarina's strangling me!" They hung holy relics round his neck and he was free from that torment. These [events] forced the lady to change house, and she took herself off to her cousin's house, leaving her own house in the charge of some of her female servants. On the tenth of that month, one of the servants went into the housekeeper's room and felt herself being called three times by Katarina.

She went to pieces in an excess of fear, and the rest of the female staff urged her to call upon our Lord for help and to go back into the room with a lighted holy candle. She chose two of the women who seemed to be bolder than the rest and went back, feeling secure. But the dead woman told her to send the other women away, get rid of the candle, because it was causing her pain, and stay there alone. Katarina then started to discharge flames, along with an unbelievable stench, from every joint in her body. She was burning from head to foot and had a band of fire, as it were, round her, eight or ten fingers wide, which extended right down to the ground. At the sight of this apparition, the servant began to tremble and turn white, and the unfortunate dead woman said to her, "Come here! How many times have I summoned you!" Almost half-dead [with fear], the servant replied, "Holy Jesus, who would not be terrified at the sight of you?" The moment she said this, there came down into that place a very beautiful child, dressed in white, who urged the servingwoman to lay aside her fear, take courage, and note carefully what Katarina was [going to] say to her, so that she could tell other people and atone for all her sins by [going to] confession as soon as she left that place.

Then Katarina spoke as follows. "Please be aware that I have been delivered up to Hell and subjected to the heaviest of punishments because when I went to the priest to confess my sins, I told him only those which were not very serious-that I was a chatter-box and talkative, prone to anger, and other things of that kindbut I said absolutely nothing about my wanton behaviour and my habitual sex with young men. Learn, then, to make a good confession and not keep silent about anything you have done wrong. I am impressing this on you because I have been commanded to do so, and I am forced to be frank about this as an example to others."

Then they heard the bell ringing for the Angelus and the dead woman quickly drew back into a corner [of the room] and vanished. But the angel-because the serving-woman was convinced the child she had seen was an angel-told her to go away home, and that is what she did.'

I decided to leave this well-attested anecdote till last because of kinds of apparition come into it: angels, St Mary Magdalene, an evil spirit looking like an 'Aithiopian', and a damned soul in an assumed body-not, I think, its own, but one made of air in the likeness of its own body.

they transform themselves into an angel of light, and into the blessed Virgin Mother of God, as happened in Bordeaux-I know this happened because I was living there at the time⁴⁵²

<div align="center"><b>The Minorite Monk's Apparition in Zamora</b></div>
<div align="center">"Martin Del Rio - Investigations Into Magic Volume 2" Pages 178</div>
and this once happened to a monk in the Dominican house in Zamora. He had entered into this pact with a Minorite, and after a number of days [the Minorite] appeared to his fellow-covenanter, who was laying tables at the time, and said he was carrying a fire of atonement around with him. As evidence of his torture, he pressed his hand on a thick wooden table and made a very deep burn-mark on it. I have been told by eye-witnesses that the scorch-mark of a hand still exists on the table and, as a perpetual reminder of what happened, has been covered with a small piece of iron lattice-work. (Father Antonio of Siena writes in his history of the Dominicans that one can have no doubts about this incident at all).

<div align="center"><b>St Lutgard's Precaution Against Deception</b></div>
<div align="center">"Martin Del Rio - Investigations Into Magic Volume 2" Pages 178</div>
When St Lutgard told a nun that if she were to die first, she would visit her, she added that she would first say the Benedicite, the Lord\'s prayer, and the angelic greeting [Hail Mary], \'so that\', she said, \'the Devil cannot introduce any deception, as he usually does.\' (See op.cit. Book 2).

<div align="center"><b>Ignes Fatui at St Audomar</b></div>
<div align="center">"Martin Del Rio - Investigations Into Magic Volume 2" Pages 179</div>
I have seen several such things at the shrine of St Audomar in St-Omer. They also exist in Italy, and ancient authors have told us about them in different places-on Lake Vadimo, on the ager Caecubus, and in Rieti.

<div align="center"><b>The Glowing Coculium in Peru</b></div>
<div align="center">"Martin Del Rio - Investigations Into Magic Volume 2" Pages 179</div>
and a small Indian creature, a member of the glow-worm family, but larger, like a scarab-beetle, which shines with its whole body, but especially with its eyes which are enormous in comparison with its little body, and pour out so much light that people are in the habit of reading and writing by it. [The natives] call it \'coculium\'. It shines with the light of four little stars together, and if anyone smears his hands and face with them, he looks like a burning, frightening ghost [spectrum]. (See [Pedro] Cieza [de León], History of Peru Part 2, chapter 30).

<div align="center"><b>Sulla's Vision of Goats' Heads</b></div>

<div align="center"><b>The Child's Extraordinary Noises from Suffocation</b></div>
<div align="center">"Martin Del Rio - Investigations Into Magic Volume 2" Pages 179-180</div>
Sometimes unskilled physicians are tricked by the extraordinary sounds made by a child from the suffocation of the womb, \'when\', says Cornelius Gemma in Book 1, chapter 7 of his Cosmocratic Art, \'the arteries have been inflated and enlarged by a poisoned gust of air and are then contracted along their length, the result is that one hears extraordinary noises coming from deep within the intestines, now like the croaking of frogs, now like the hissing of snakes, now like the cawing of crows, the crowing of cocks, the barking of dogs, etc. But this tells one there is an emergency because of the relative size of the passages and the [amount] of air which is bursting out\'.

<div align="center"><b>King Kenneth's Glowing Angels Deception</b></div>
<div align="center">"Martin Del Rio - Investigations Into Magic Volume 2" Pages 180</div>
According to [Hector] Boethius [Boece], this is how King Kenneth of Scotland conquered the Picts by whom he had been conquered. While the commanders of his army were sleeping at night, he sent servants to them, dressed in shining scale-armour and holding in their hands spears made from rotten wood which glows in the dark, in order to encourage his [commanders] to engage bravely with the enemy, saying that they themselves had been sent by God to guarantee victory. The commanders believed they were angels, enthusiastically attacked the Picts, and massacred them.

<div align="center"><b>Glowing Ghosts from Crabs and Tortoises in Cemeteries</b></div>
